Merge: 8258a874 05f1a5bd
Author: VWoeltjen <victor.woeltjen@nasa.gov>

    Merge pull request #278 from VWoeltjen/mct172
    
    [Canvas] Avoid null TransferHandler

commit 05f1a5bde8b837c289f84409f3c5189938aaf581
Author: Victor Woeltjen <victor.woeltjen@nasa.gov>
Date:   Tue Mar 18 15:56:14 2014 -0700

    [Canvas] Avoid null TransferHandler
    
    Transfer handlers on Inspector labels
    are not necessary after inspected view
    is clear, as there is nothing to transfer.
    However, Swing's event-handling does go
    back to inform the original transfer
    handler that an event has completed; if
    this happens after the component's
    transfer handler has been nullified,
    nasa/mct#172 results.
    
    To avoid this issue, instead of nullifying
    the transfer handler, simply introduce
    checks such that it becomes inert when
    there is no view in the Inspector.

4	5	canvas/src/main/java/gov/nasa/arc/mct/canvas/view/PanelInspector.java
36	3	canvas/src/test/java/gov/nasa/arc/mct/canvas/view/PanelInspectorTest.java

    (which includes adding My Sandbox as a bootstrap

    absence of My Sandbox on first run see in
    nasa/mct#245.

commit f34fecfeabf88859d1c6bc72c5e5890c60bc2158
Author: Victor Woeltjen <victor.woeltjen@nasa.gov>
Date:   Fri Feb 28 12:51:51 2014 -0800

    [Platform] Avoid NPE on getMySandbox
    
    Remove risk of hitting NPE on getMySandbox in
    PlatformImpl. Stored reference to sandbox is
    obtained during call to getBootstrapComponents,
    but if that has not been called when getMySandbox
    is needed, an NPE occurs.
    
    This is significant for nasa/MCT-Plugins#134,
    which requires some deployment-specific additions
    to My Sandbox; since the most obvious place to
    do this is at bootstrapping time, e.g. before
    or during the first call to PlatformImpl's
    getBootstrapComponents.

commit ccfa4389174f8203ad288e3ecb1005d1a38693b8
Author: Victor Woeltjen <victor.woeltjen@nasa.gov>
Date:   Tue Dec 31 09:58:22 2013 -0800

    [Save All] Allow Save without ObjectManager
    
    Consolidating Save and Save All behavior
    into one action, for nasa/mct#131.
    
    Save All (which has become the consolidated
    Save) previously required an ObjectManager
    capability to be present, as the presence
    thereof was what distinguish Save situations
    from Save All situations. This change allows
    for the ObjectManager capability to be
    unavailable, in which case the action
    functions as te per-object save.
    
    Additionally, rules for action eligibility
    are relaxed to allow Save when not all
    objects are writeable (e.g. because someone
    else owns the object.) Objects which cannot
    be written are not saved.

34	16	platform/src/main/java/gov/nasa/arc/mct/gui/actions/ObjectsSaveAllAction.java

    universally the action they wanted to

    seemed like the familiar choice.)

commit ca11c48834f05b9a4486ac36c889f79ce4019d05
Author: Victor Woeltjen <victor.woeltjen@nasa.gov>
Date:   Wed Dec 18 08:34:20 2013 -0800

    [Persistence] Keep bootstrap cache up-to-date during start up
    
    Fix for nasa/mct#111 involves a "step-behind cache"
    for bootstrap components which is sometimes behind
    the latest result from the database. This is
    acceptable during operation or reuse of MCT, when
    the set of bootstrap components changes very
    rarely and is a background delay is unlikely to
    be noticed. However, during startup of MCT on a
    new database (particularly when configured to
    automatically add users, or when plugins introduce
    new bootstrap components) this can lead to errors
    which emerge from the failure to recognize
    bootstrap components just after they were
    introduced.
    
    Addressed here:
    
    * Pre-populate the bootstrap cache once when
      the persistence service is activated.
    * Explicitly the cache whenever components are
      tagged as bootstraps from the running
      instance of MCT.

commit a83e68a11bee4a15afb59a100cb075cdb94c43f1
Author: Victor Woeltjen <victor.woeltjen@nasa.gov>
Date:   Wed Dec 11 10:12:32 2013 -0800

    [Persistence] Use thread pool for step-behind cache
    
    Use a thread pool in step-behind cache to avoid creating an
    excessive number of background threads.
    
    While the existing time delay provides some throttling
    with regard to the number of actual look-ups initiated, it
    is not a guarantee against rampant thread creation,
    particularly where time delay is less than the time taken
    to complete the underlying lookup operation.

commit bbb7572b423966099ff9814b773e928b7606e886
Author: Victor Woeltjen <victor.woeltjen@nasa.gov>
Date:   Tue Dec 10 16:43:36 2013 -0800

    [Persistence] Add Step-Behind Cache
    
    Introduces a 'Step-Behind Cache' to handle
    custom queries. This returns values which are
    effectively one step behind the results given
    by the real operation being performed.
    
    This is used to provide quick answers for
    custom database lookups (such as getting
    all users) while still receiving updates
    eventually, without incurring the cost of
    polling. This is useful in cases (such as
    getting a list of users) where the data
    changes infrequently, and where it is
    acceptable to be somewhat out-of-step with
    the ground truth.
    
    This addresses the remaining known cause
    of latency in nasa/mct#111.

commit febec705d9346a0dc6b34b927b910bc296455eaf
Author: Victor Woeltjen <victor.woeltjen@nasa.gov>
Date:   Tue Dec 10 15:07:28 2013 -0800

    [Persistence] Cache ids of bootstraps
    
    Bootstrap components are used to inform specific
    policies for mutating components. Because
    databasePersistence uses some custom SQL to
    identify bootstrap components, the component
    cache is effectively circumvented, meaning that
    every time bootstrap components are looked at a
    database interaction occurs. This has bad
    latency implications when triggered from policy,
    particularly where database latency is high,
    and has been identified as a contributing factor
    to nasa/mct#111.
    
    This change caches the list of component IDs
    found to be bootstrap components on first
    invocation, and looks up via those IDs
    subsequently. Looking up by ID does use the
    component cache, thus avoiding the extra cost of
    database access while still remaining at least
    as up-to-date as the component cache itself.

42	23	databasePersistence/src/main/java/gov/nasa/arc/mct/dbpersistence/service/PersistenceServiceImpl.java

    result in redundant updates but should
    avoid missed updates, except in cases of
    extreme latency.

commit 45f19d056b9ab00f75480a0595e587ab429aa691
Author: Victor Woeltjen <victor.woeltjen@nasa.gov>
Date:   Thu Oct 10 15:12:22 2013 -0700

    [Persistence] Specify last modified (derby compatibility)
    
    Apache Derby does not support
    ON UPDATE CURRENT_TIMESTAMP, which is used
    in prior commits to match modified time to
    that read from database. As an alternative,
    use time read from database during polling
    to estimate the current database time when
    persisting components (adjusting for the
    local time elapsed since the database time
    was last read.)

commit fa68e850cb7e82eedc343521ee9439736310e2a3
Author: Victor Woeltjen <victor.woeltjen@nasa.gov>
Date:   Thu Oct 10 11:30:14 2013 -0700

    [Persistence] Evict cached children on update from database
    
    Referenced component (or, more specifically,
    ComponentSpec object) collections are stored
    in the L2 cache as of #48; this caching is
    useful in reducing latency related to repeated
    loading of referenced components, particularly
    where the database is accessed over a network.
    However, the L2 cache is not refreshed by
    changes to the parent ComponentSpec, causing
    child references to fall out of date, which
    results in nasa/mct#134 and some cases of
    nasa/mct#110.
    
    This fixes the issue by evicting these
    collections explicitly for any components
    which are updated from the database. This
    allows unchanged components to continue to
    use the cache, retaining the performance
    benefits when viewing objects.
    
    The explicit references to Hibernate involved
    introduce a dependency which may not be
    necessary; this is addressed by followup
    issue nasa/mct#212.

10	1	databasePersistence/src/main/java/gov/nasa/arc/mct/dbpersistence/service/PersistenceServiceImpl.java

commit 6e76e53d013917701d514eb2718a83abb30dcc6c
Author: Victor Woeltjen <victor.woeltjen@nasa.gov>
Date:   Wed Oct 9 19:09:52 2013 -0700

    [Persistence] Nullify lastModified before update
    
    Set lastModified to null before persisting,
    but specify that it is not nullable (such
    that CURRENT_TIMESTAMP is used instead.)
    This ensures that lastModified always uses
    the database's version of the current time
    and always records this at the time the
    object is updated. Object polling also
    uses CURRENT_TIMESTAMP from DB, so if this
    is not updated or recorded from different
    clocks then component updates may be missed,
    resulting in nasa/mct#110 and nasa/mct#134.

commit 11a79db38138884f3f28cdfd7dde8ef921b83c61
Author: Victor Woeltjen <victor.woeltjen@nasa.gov>
Date:   Mon Sep 30 16:30:31 2013 -0700

    [Save All] Back explicit object manager map
    
    Use a map of id to component to track modified
    objects in the explicit object manager. This
    means that if multiple versions of the same
    component are explicitly added as modified
    objects, only the latest is actually returned
    in a subsequent getModifiedObjects. This
    avoids Save All ambiguities in cases where
    multiple versions of the same object are
    returned in getModifiedObjects.

commit 4e3e7ed0f47b8d52995d84beeeacd058bd0ad6b3
Author: Victor Woeltjen <victor.woeltjen@nasa.gov>
Date:   Thu Sep 26 15:17:32 2013 -0700

    [Launcher] Pop up user dialog lazily
    
    When MCT is launched with no user specified,
    the DefaultIdentityManager should pop up a
    dialog of available users. However, the
    persistence service is used to determine
    which users are available, and this service
    not necessarily been created at the time the
    default identity manager is created (due
    to bundle ordering.) When persistence is
    null, nasa/mct#199 occurs.
    
    In this change, default identity manager
    does not try to identify the current user
    until the first time getCurrentUser is
    invoked. This occurs from LaunchMCTService,
    which depends upon the PersistenceService
    having been bound (so it is guaranteed to
    be available.)

40	22	platform/src/main/java/gov/nasa/arc/mct/identitymgr/impl/DefaultIdentityManager.java

commit adc63ec9e390456a520b41dcb5c56241939ea687
Author: Victor Woeltjen <victor.woeltjen@nasa.gov>
Date:   Mon Sep 23 16:17:13 2013 -0700

    [Views] Disregard view type when testing info equality
    
    Certain set operations upon ViewInfo objects
    are contingent upon the treatment of ViewInfo
    objects describing the same class as equal,
    even if they apply to different view types.
    Failure to exhibit this sort of equality is
    the root cause of nasa/mct#195.
    
    This change removes consideration of view
    type and hashCode from equals (this was
    added erroneously in a previous commit
    triggering the regression.)

0	2	mctcore/src/main/java/gov/nasa/arc/mct/services/component/ViewInfo.java

commit 9c0bcefc5d92305651ce3e463cd49c952d6d9220
Author: Victor Woeltjen <victor.woeltjen@nasa.gov>
Date:   Mon Sep 23 14:21:04 2013 -0700

    [Tests] Fix scatter plot test
    
    Scatter plot test was failing on auto-expand
    behavior after merge with new controls for
    non-time non-time plots. This was due to the
    associated bounds managers, which feature an
    optimization based on the assumption that
    data will not be received (by the plot) in
    the middle of an existing set (only prepend
    or append is expected.)
    
    As this is currently an accepted limitation
    of plots, unit tests are amended to ensure
    that data which is expected to expand the
    plot includes time stamps which have not
    been previously exercised.

commit 2bd6dec93d576916ca6f0180c3a0b1cb71add88d
Author: Victor Woeltjen <victor.woeltjen@nasa.gov>
Date:   Mon Sep 16 13:02:03 2013 -0700

    [Ownership] Prevent ownership change on bootstrap comps
    
    In nasa/mct#123 the user is able to change ownership
    of My Sandbox, which means they subsequently cannot
    edit their own sandbox. Worse, when they restart MCT
    they see no sandbox at all.
    
    This adds a check to prevent this. When ownership
    mutability is being determined, consult the list
    of bootstrap components - this is the list of
    components seen by the user in the User Environment.
    Categorically disallow changes of ownership to any
    of these (this includes both My Sandbox, and any
    future top-level components introduced, as these
    are presumed to be inherently tied to the user. An
    example of a top-level component not yet introduced
    is User Tags, described in nasa/MCT-Plugins#39.)

11	3	mctcore/src/main/java/gov/nasa/arc/mct/platform/spi/RoleAccess.java

commit b57f7b4df682c2abe38c072aab27b519dde51f9f
Author: Victor Woeltjen <victor.woeltjen@nasa.gov>
Date:   Fri Sep 13 17:02:50 2013 -0700

    [Database] Allow configuration of polling interval
    
    Reduces database polling interval, and allows
    configuration on a per-user basis. This addresses
    both perceived and actual issues with object
    modification:
    
    * nasa/mct#54 notes that object deletion seems
      to take a long time. Root cause is that the
      Browse area is refreshed by database polling,
      which takes place at a longer interval (3s).
      Decreasing this interval means that the user
      sees the consequences of their action sooner.
    * nasa/mct#132 occurs when the user switches
      back and forth between objects faster than
      the poll interval. This can cause an object
      to be flagged as stale because changes from
      one save have not made their way back to
      the Browse area. While this still may occur
      with a shorter polling interval, the odds
      of the user observing this decrease
      significantly.
    * nasa/mct#111 describes latency issues, some
      of which may be related to the poll
      interval. (It is unlikely, however, that
      menu item latency is related to this.)

14	2	databasePersistence/src/main/java/gov/nasa/arc/mct/dbpersistence/service/PersistenceServiceImpl.java
3	0	platform-assembly/src/main/resources/properties/mysql.properties
6	0	platform-assembly/src/main/resources/properties/persistence.properties

commit d7b668548c941acd31988a8c73f3cb07c8109c20
Author: Victor Woeltjen <victor.woeltjen@nasa.gov>
Date:   Wed Sep 4 11:21:50 2013 -0700

    [Inspector] Make view-setting part of ViewProvider
    
    Add the ability to set contained views to the
    ViewProvider interface (an appropriate
    corollary to its existing get method). This
    method may reject changes - by default, View
    simply returns false to indicate that the
    change has been ignored.
    
    This is to facilitate the decoupling of the
    Inspector view from the control used to
    switch views (view switching is a
    cross-cutting concern, occurring in multiple
    Inspector implementations and desirable in a
    fiew contexts.)
    
    This ultimately serves to support combo box
    style switcher described in nasa/mct#135

commit b7fb18c0108c19e181ef2aa9b2a1ef8339723803
Author: Victor Woeltjen <victor.woeltjen@nasa.gov>
Date:   Wed Aug 28 17:15:34 2013 -0700

    [Icons] Algorithmically generate icons if not provided
    
    Underlying issue for icon revampment is inability to
    easily distinguish objects of different types if they
    do not have custom icons. Adding custom icons is the
    best part of the solution, but this additionally adds
    procedurally generated icons based on component type
    hash codes which emulate the general look of the
    default component. These do not clearly indicate
    what type of thing a thing is, but do make it easy to
    identify when two things are or are not of the same
    type.

Author: Ron van Hoof <Ron.vanHoof@nasa.gov>
Date:   Fri Jan 18 14:40:51 2013 -0500

    [MCT-3811] Fix for Canvas on canvas: Panel cannot be
    selected, drag-drop throws exception.
    Fixed the issue of selection of panel with a canvas. The issue was
    that the selection was cleared by a call to panel.clearSelections. Moved
    this call in front of the panel selection.
    Fixed the exception when performing a DnD of the canvas panel in the
    canvas. An endless loop was initiated between panel and canvas for
    selection changes when clearing selections. Now testing whether
    any selection needs to be cleared, if not, no clearing is initiated
    preventing the infinite loop.

If a component does not allow the platform info view to show up (e.g., policy controlled), then whichever the first viewinfo returned by AbstractComponent.getViewInfos() will show in the inspector. commit 51fc22a49aa8c62b5a3309fb9a93f704b73780bf
Author: Dan Berrios <daniel.c.berrios@nasa.gov>
Date:   Fri Jul 6 13:55:58 2012 -0700

    [MCT-3605] [multi] Error is wrongly flagged when adding rules to
    embedded multi
    [MCT-3603] [multi] Misplaced error
    [MCT-3589] Users can create objects via context menu even if a
    composition policy exists and says they shouldn't be able to
    The approach is to create a temporary component and check it against
    target component using composition policy. If it fails, then don't add

    inside a multi that doesn't have a feed view, fixing the reported multi
    composition-related bugs.

commit 6f84d4236c6000def2634293f54c6afe4da84290
Author: nshi <nija.shi@nasa.gov>
Date:   Thu Jun 28 15:09:10 2012 -0700

    Fixed MCT-3682 [Descendants] Reordering components causes duplicate
    component references to appear in the same collection. Because the
    list of child components is soft-referenced, a different list of
    child components may be retrieved each time getComponents() is called.
    So upon reordering/manipulting child components, we get a snapshot of
    the child list and work on that list, instead of calling
    getComponents() multiple times.
